herd of buffalo ` there may be other ' say the gomasta and peer into every bush we go slowly on the elephant now shewed decide symptom of dislike and a reluctance to approach a particular dense clump of grass a sound whack on the head however make she quicken she step and thrust the long stalk aside she discover for we three blinking little cub brother of the defunct and doubtless part of the same litter they eye be scarcely open and they lay huddle together like three enormous striped kitten and spat at we and bristle they little moustache much as a angry cat would do all the four be male it be not long ere i have they carefully wrap in the mahout 's blanket overjoy at we good fortune we leave the excited buffalo still execute they singular war-dance and the angry tigress rob of she whelp consume she soul in baffled fury we hear she roaring through the night close to camp and on my friend ' arrival we beat she up next morning and she fall pierce by three bullet after a fierce and determine charge we come upon she across the nullah and she mind be evidently make up to fight nearly all the villager have turn out with the line of elephant before we have time to order they away she come down upon the line roaring furiously and bound over the long grass -- a most magnificent sight my first bullet take she full in the chest and before she could make good she charge a ball each from pat and captain g settle she career she be beautifully striped and rather large for a tigress measure nine foot three inch it be now a question with I how to rear the three interesting orphan we think a slut from some of the village would prove the best wet nurse and try accordingly to get one but could not in the meantime a unhappy goat be pounce on and the three young-tiger take to she teat as if ` to the manner bear ' the poor nanny scream tremendously at first sight of they but she soon get accustom to they and when they grow a little bigger she would often playfully butt at they with she horn the little brute thrive wonderfully and soon develop such a appetite that i have to get no less than six goat to satisfy they constant thirst i keep the cub for over two month and i shall not soon forget the excitement i cause when my boat stop at sahribgunge and my goat tiger cub and attendant form a procession from the ghat or landing-place to the railway station soldier guard engineer traveller and crowd of native surround I and at every station the guard 's van with my novel menagerie be the center of attraction i sell the cub to jamrach 's agent in calcutta for a very satisfactory price two of they be very powerful finely marked handsome animal the third have always be sickly have frequent convulsion and die a few day after i sell it i be afterwards tell that the milk diet be a mistake and that i should have feed they on raw meat however i be very well satisfy on the whole with the result of my adventure i have another in the same part of the country which at the time be a pretty good test of the state of my nerve i be camp out at the village of purindaha on the edge of a gloomy sal forest which be report to contain numerous leopard the villager be a mixed lot of low-caste hindoo and nepaulese settler they have be fight with the factory and would not pay up they rent and i be try with every probability of success to make a amicable arrangement with they at all event i have so far win they round that they be willing to talk to I they come to the tent and listen quietly and except on the subject of rent we get on in the most friendly manner it be the middle of April the heat be intense the whole atmosphere have that coppery look which denote extreme heat and the air be load with fine yellow dust which the daily west wind bear on its fever laden wing to disturb the lung and temper of all good christian the _ kanat _ or canvas wall of the tent have all be take down for coolness and my camp bed lay in one corner open all round to the outside air but only sheltered from the dew it have be a busy day i have be go over account and talk to the villager till i be really hoarse after a light dinner i lay down on my bed but it be too close and hot to sleep by and bye the various sound die out the tom-toming cease in the village my servant suspend they low muttered gossip round the cook 's fire wrap themselves in they white cloth and drop into slumber ` toby ' ` nettle ' ` whisky ' ` pincher ' and my other terrier resemble so many curled-up hairy ball and be in the land of dream occasionally a owl would give a melancholy hoot from the forest or a screech owl would raise a momentary and damnable din at interval the tinkle of a cow-bell sound faintly in the distance i toss restlessly think of various thing till i must have drop off into a uneasy fitful sleep i know not how long i have be doze but of a sudden i feel myself wide awake though with my eye yet firmly close i be conscious of some terrible unknown impending danger i have experience the same feeling before on wake from a nightmare but i know that the danger now be real i feel a shrink horror a terrible and nameless fear and for the life of I i could not move hand or foot i be lie on my side and could distinctly hear the thumping of my heart a cold sweat break out behind my ear and over my neck and chest i could analyze my every feeling and i know there be some presence in the tent and that i be in instant and imminent peril suddenly in the distance a pariah dog give a prolonged melancholy howl as if this have break the spell which have hitherto bind I i open my eye and within ten inch of my face there be a handsome leopardess gaze steadily at I we eye meet and how long we confront each other i know not it must have be some minute she eye contract and expand the pupil elongate and then open out into a round lustrous globe i could see the lithe tail oscillate at its extreme tip with a gentle wave motion like that of a cat when hunting bird in the garden i seem to possess no will i believe i be under a species of fascination but we continue we steady stare at each other just then there be a movement by some of the horse the leopard slowly turn she head and i grasp the revolver which lay under my pillow the beautiful spotted monster turn she head for a instant and shew she tooth and then with one bind go through the open side of the tent i fire two shot which be answer with a roar the din that follow would have frighten the devil it be a beautiful clear night with a moon at the full and everything shew as plainly as at noonday the servant utter exclamation of terror the terrier go into a agony of yelp and bark the horse snort and try to get loose and my chowkeydar who have be asleep on he watch think a band of dacoit be on we begin lay round he with he staff shout _ chor chor lagga lagga lagga _ that be ` thief thief lay on lay on lay on ' the leopard be hit and evidently in a terrible temper she halt not thirty pace from the tent beside a jhamun tree and seem undecided whether to go on or return and wreak she vengeance on I that moment decide she fate i snatch down my express rifle which be hang in two loop above my bed and shoot she right through the heart i never understand how she could have make she way past dog servant horse and watchman right into the tent without raise some alarm it must have be more from curiosity than any hostile design i know that my nerve be very rudely shake but i become the hero of the purindaha villager i believe that my night adventure with the leopardess do more to bring they round to a settlement than all my eloquence and figure the river koosee on the bank of which and in the long grass plain adjacent most of the incident i have record take place take its rise at the base of mount everest and after drain nearly the whole of eastern nepaul emerge by a deep gorge from the hill at the north-west corner of purneah the stream run with extreme velocity it be know as a snow stream the water be always cold and generally of a milky color contain much fine white sand no sooner do it leave its rocky bed than it tear through the flat country by numerous channel it be subject to very sudden rise a premonitory warning of these be generally give the water become of a turbid almost blood-like color sometimes i have see the river rise over thirty foot in twenty-four hour the melting of the snow often make a rage torrent level from bank to bank where only a few hour before a horse could have ford the stream without wet the girth of the saddle in 1876 the largest channel be a swift broad stream call the dhaus the river be very capricious seldom flow for any length of time in one channel this be owe in great measure to the amount of silt it carry with it from the hill in its impetuous progress to the plain in these dry watercourse among the sand ridge beside the humid marshy hollow and among the thick strip of grass jungle tiger be always to be find they be much less numerous now however than formerly as a rule there be no shelter in these water-worn flood-ravaged tract and sultry jungle occasionally a few straggle plantain tree a clump of sickly-looking bamboo a cluster of tall shadowless palm mark the site of a desert village all else be wave grass withered and dry the village inhabit mostly by a few cowherd boatman and rice-farmer be scatter at wide interval in the shooting season and when the hot wind be blow the only shadow on the plain be that cast by the dense volume of lurid smoke rise in blind cloud from the jungle fire accord to the season animal life fluctuate strangely during the rain when the river be in full flood and much of the country submerge most of the animal migrate to the north buffalo and wild pig alone keep possession of the higher ridge in the neighborhood of they usual haunt the contrast present on these plain at different season of the year be most remarkable in march and April they be parch up brown and dead great black patch show the track of a destroy fire the fine brown ash from the burnt grass penetrate the eye and nostril and sweeping along in eddy and blind cloud they then look the very picture of a untenable waste a sea of desolation whose limit blend in the extreme distance with the shimmering coppery horizon in the rainy season these arid-looking waste be cover with tall-plumed reed-like wave grass vary from two to ten foot in height stretch in a unbroken sweep as far as the eye can reach except where a abrupt line shew that the swift river have its treacherous course after the rain progress through the jungle be dangerous quicksand and bed of tenacious mud impede one at every step the rich vegetation spring up green and vigorous with a rapidity only to be see in the tropics but what a glorious hunting ground what a preserve for nimrod deer forest or heathered moor can never compete with the old koosee derah for abundance of game and thrilling excitement in sport my genial happy loyal comrade too -- while memory last the recollection of you joyous frank warm-hearted comradeship shall never fade chapter xxvi remark on gun -- how to cure skin -- different recipe -- conclusion my remark on gun shall be brief the true sportsman have many facility for acquire the best information on a choice of weapon for large game perhaps nothing can equal the express rifle my own trusty weapon be a ' 500 bear very plain with a pistol grip point blank up to 180 yard make by murcott of the haymarket from whom i have buy over twenty gun every one of which turn out a splendid weapon my next favorite be a no 12 breachloader very light but strong and carefully finish it have a side snap action with rebound lock and be the quickest gun to fire and reload i ever possess i buy it from the same maker although it be manufacture by ww greener avoid a cheap gun as you would avoid a cheap jew pedlar a good name be above riches so far as a gun be concerned and when you have a good gun take as much care of it as you would of a good wife they be both equally rare a expensive gun be not necessarily a good one but a cheap gun be very seldom trustworthy have a portable handy black leather case keep you gun always clean bright and free from rust after every day 's shooting see that the barrel and lock be carefully clean and oil nothing be better for this purpose than rangoon oil for preserve horn a little scrape and varnish be all that be require while in camp it be a good plan to rub they with deer or pig or tiger fat as it keep they from crack to clean a tiger 's or other skull if there be a nest of ant near the camp place the skull in they immediate vicinity some recommend put in water till the particle of flesh rot or till the skull be clear by the fish a strong solution of caustic water may be use if you wish to get the bone clean very quickly some put the skull in quicklime but it have a tendency to make the bone splinter and it be difficult to keep the tooth from get loose and drop out the best but slowest plan be to fix they in mechanically by wire or white lead a good preservative be to wash or paint they with a very strong solution of fine lime and water to cure skin i know no better recipe than the one adopt by my trainer in the art of _ shibar _ the brother s i can not do better than give a description of the process in the word of george himself ` skin the animal in the usual way cut from the corner of the mouth down the throat and along the belly a white stripe or border generally run along the belly this should be leave as nearly as possible equal on both side carefully cut the fleshy part off the lip and ball of the toe and foot clean away every particle of fatty or fleshy matter that may still adhere to the skin peg it out on the ground with the hair side undermost when thoroughly scrape clean of all extraneous matter on the inner surface get a bucket or tub of buttermilk which be call by the native _ dahye _ or _ mutha _ it be a favorite article of diet with they cheap and plentiful dip the skin in this and keep it well and entirely submerge by place some heavy weight on it it should be submerge fully three inch in the tub of buttermilk ` after two day in the milk bath take it out and peg it as before now take a smooth oval rubbing-board about twelve inch long five round and about a inch thick in the middle and scrub the skin heartily with this instrument on its lower surface it should be cut in groove semicircular in shape half a inch wide and one inch apart during scrub use plenty of pure water to remove filth in about half a hour the pinkish-white color will disappear and the skin will appear white with a blackish tinge underneath this be the true hide ` again submerge in the buttermilk bath for twenty-four hour and get a man to tread on it in every possible way folding it and unfold it till all have be thoroughly work ` take it out again peg out and scrub it as before after which wash the whole hide well in clear water never mind if the skin look rotten it be really not so ` when wash put it into a tub in which you have first place a mixture consist of half a ounce of alum to each gallon of water soak the skin in this mixture for about six hour take it up occasionally to drain a little this be sufficient to cure you skin and clean it ' the tanning remain to be do ` get four pound of babool tamarind or dry oak bark -lrb- the babool be a kind of acacia and be easily procurable as the tamarind also be -rrb- boil the bark in two gallon of water till it be reduce to one half the quantity add to this nine gallon of fresh water and in this solution souse the skin for two or three or four day ` the hair have be set by the soak in alum the skin will tan more quickly and if the tan be occasionally rub into the pore of the skin it will be a improvement you can tell when the tanning be complete by the color the skin assume when this satisfy the eye take it out and drain on a rod when nearly dry it should be curry with olive oil or clarify butter if require for wear but if only for floor cover or carriage rug the english currier ' common ` dubbin ' sell by shopkeeper be best this operation which must be do on the inner side only be simple ` another simple recipe and one which answer well be this mix together of the best english soap four ounce arsenic two and a half grain camphor two ounce alum half a ounce saltpetre half a ounce boil the whole and keep stir in a half-pint of distilled water over a very slow fire for from ten to fifteen minute apply when cool with a sponge a little sweet oil may be rub on the skin after they be dry ` another good method be to apply arsenical soap which may be make as follow : powdered arsenic two pound camphor five ounce white soap slice thin two pound salt of tartar twelve dram chalk or powdered fine lime four ounce add a small quantity of water first to the soap put over a gentle fire and keep stir when melt add the lime and tartar and thoroughly mix next add the arsenic keep up a constant motion and lastly the camphor the camphor should first be reduce to a powder by means of a little spirit of wine and should be add to the mess after it have be take off the fire ` this preparation must be keep in a well-stoppered jar or properly close pot when ready the soap should be of the consistency of devonshire cream to use add water till it become of the consistency of clear rich soup ' i have now finish my book it have be pleasant to I to write down these recollection ever since i begin my task death have be busy and the rank of my friend have be sadly thin fail health have drive I from my old shooting grounds and in sunny australium i have be try to recruit the energy enervate by the burning climate of indium that my dear old planter friend may have as kindly recollection of ` the maorus ' as he have of they be what i ardently hope that i may yet get back to share in the sport pastime joy and social delight of mofussil life in indium be what i chiefly desire if this volume meet the approbation of the public i may be tempt to draw further on a well-stocked memory and gossip afresh on indian life indian experience and indian sport meantime courteous reader farewell end of the project gutenberg ebook of sport and work on the nepaul frontier by jame inglis
